Based on this\n    49→  /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\n    50→  /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\n    51→  /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\n    52→  /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\n    53→  ///\n    54→  enum TypeID {\n    55→    // PrimitiveTypes\n    56→    HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\n    57→    BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\n    58→    FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\n    59→    DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\n    60→    X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\n    61→    FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\n    62→    PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\n    63→    VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\n    64→    LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\n    65→    MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\n    66→    X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\n    67→    TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\n    68→\n    69→    // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\n    70→    IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\n    71→    FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\n    72→    PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\n    73→    StructTyID,         ///< Structures\n    74→    ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\n    75→    FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\n    76→    ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\n    77→    TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\n    78→    TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\n    79→  };\n    80→\n    81→private:\n    82→  /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n    83→  LLVMContext &Context;\n    84→\n    85→  TypeID   ID : 8;            // The current base type of this type.\n    86→  unsigned SubclassData : 24; // Space for subclasses to store data.\n    87→                              // Note that this should be synchronized with\n    88→                              // MAX_INT_BITS value in IntegerType class.\n    89→\n    90→protected:\n    91→  friend class LLVMContextImpl;\n    92→\n    93→  explicit Type(LLVMContext &C, TypeID tid)\n    94→    : Context(C), ID(tid), SubclassData(0) {}\n    95→  ~Type() = default;\n    96→\n    97→  unsigned getSubclassData() const { return SubclassData; }\n    98→\n    99→  void setSubclassData(unsigned val) {\n   100→    SubclassData = val;\n   101→    // Ensure we don't have any accidental truncation.\n   102→    assert(getSubclassData() == val && \"Subclass data too large for field\");\n   103→  }\n   104→\n   105→  /// Keeps track of how many Type*'s there are in the ContainedTys list.\n   106→  unsigned NumContainedTys = 0;\n   107→\n   108→  /// A pointer to the array of Types contained by this Type. For example, this\n   109→  /// includes the arguments of a function type, the elements of a structure,\n   110→  /// the pointee of a pointer, the element type of an array, etc. This pointer\n   111→  /// may be 0 for types that don't contain other types (Integer, Double,\n   112→  /// Float).\n   113→  Type * const *ContainedTys = nullptr;\n   114→\n   115→public:\n   116→  /// Print the current type.\n   117→  /// Omit the type details if \\p NoDetails == true.\n   118→  /// E.g., let %st = type { i32, i16 }\n   119→  /// When \\p NoDetails is true, we only print %st.\n   120→  /// Put differently, \\p NoDetails prints the type as if\n   121→  /// inlined with the operands when printing an instruction.\n   122→  LLVM_ABI void print(raw_ostream &O, bool IsForDebug = false,\n   123→                      bool NoDetails = false) const;\n   124→\n   125→  LLVM_ABI void dump() const;\n   126→\n   127→  /// Return the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n   128→  LLVMContext &getContext() const { return Context; }\n   129→\n   130→  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n   131→  // Accessors for working with types.\n   132→  //\n   133→\n   134→  /// Return the type id for the type. This will return one of the TypeID enum\n   135→  /// elements defined above.\n   136→  TypeID getTypeID() const { return ID; }\n   137→\n   138→  /// Return true if this is 'void'.\n   139→  bool isVoidTy() const { return getTypeID() == VoidTyID; }\n   140→\n   141→  /// Return true if this is 'half', a 16-bit IEEE fp type.\n   142→  bool isHalfTy() const { return getTypeID() == HalfTyID; }\n   143→\n   144→  /// Return true if this is 'bfloat', a 16-bit bfloat type.\n   145→  bool isBFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID; }\n   146→\n   147→  /// Return true if this is a 16-bit float type.\n   148→  bool is16bitFPTy() const {\n   149→    return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID || getTypeID() == HalfTyID;\n   150→  }\n   151→\n   152→  /// Return true if this is 'float', a 32-bit IEEE fp type.\n   153→  bool isFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == FloatTyID; }\n   154→\n   155→  /// Return true if this is 'double', a 64-bit IEEE fp type.\n   156→  bool isDoubleTy() const { return getTypeID() == DoubleTyID; }\n   157→\n   158→  /// Return true if this is x86 long double.\n   159→  bool isX86_FP80Ty() const { return getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID; }\n   160→\n   161→  /// Return true if this is 'fp128'.\n   162→  bool isFP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == FP128TyID; }\n   163→\n   164→  /// Return true if this is powerpc long double.\n   165→  bool isPPC_FP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID; }\n   166→\n   167→  /// Return true if this is a well-behaved IEEE-like type, which has a IEEE\n   168→  /// compatible layout, and does not have non-IEEE values, such as x86_fp80's\n   169→  /// unnormal values.\n   170→  bool isIEEELikeFPTy() const {\n   171→    switch (getTypeID()) {\n   172→    case DoubleTyID:\n   173→    case FloatTyID:\n   174→    case HalfTyID:\n   175→    case BFloatTyID:\n   176→    case FP128TyID:\n   177→      return true;\n   178→    default:\n   179→      return false;\n   180→    }\n   181→  }\n   182→\n   183→  /// Return true if this is one of the floating-point types\n   184→  bool isFloatingPointTy() const {\n   185→    return isIEEELikeFPTy() || getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID ||\n   186→           getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\n   187→  }\n   188→\n   189→  /// Returns true if this is a floating-point type that is an unevaluated sum\n   190→  /// of multiple floating-point units.\n   191→  /// An example of such a type is ppc_fp128, also known as double-double, which\n   192→  /// consists of two IEEE 754 doubles.\n   193→  bool isMultiUnitFPType() const {\n   194→    return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\n   195→  }\n   196→\n   197→  LLVM_ABI const fltSemantics &getFltSemantics() const;\n   198→\n   199→  /// Return true if this is X86 AMX.\n   200→  bool isX86_AMXTy() const { return getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID; }\n   201→\n   202→  /// Return true if this is a target extension type.\n   203→  bool isTargetExtTy() const { return getTypeID() == TargetExtTyID; }\n   204→\n   205→  /// Return true if this is a target extension type with a scalable layout.\n   206→  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTargetExtTy() const;\n   207→\n   208→  /// Return true if this is a type whose size is a known multiple of vscale.\n   209→  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTy(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n   210→  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTy() const;\n   211→\n   212→  /// Return true if this type is or contains a target extension type that\n   213→  /// disallows being used as a global.\n   214→  LLVM_ABI bool\n   215→  containsNonGlobalTargetExtType(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n   216→  LLVM_ABI bool containsNonGlobalTargetExtType() const;\n   217→\n   218→  /// Return true if this type is or contains a target extension type that\n   219→  /// disallows being used as a local.\n   220→  LLVM_ABI bool\n   221→  containsNonLocalTargetExtType(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n   222→  LLVM_ABI bool containsNonLocalTargetExtType() const;\n   223→\n   224→  /// Return true if this is a FP type or a vector of FP.\n   225→  bool isFPOrFPVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isFloatingPointTy(); }\n   226→\n   227→  /// Return true if this is 'label'.\n   228→  bool isLabelTy() const { return getTypeID() == LabelTyID; }\n   229→\n   230→  /// Return true if this is 'metadata'.\n   231→  bool isMetadataTy() const { return getTypeID() == MetadataTyID; }\n   232→\n   233→  /// Return true if this is 'token'.\n   234→  bool isTokenTy() const { return getTypeID() == TokenTyID; }\n   235→\n   236→  /// Returns true if this is 'token' or a token-like target type.s\n   237→  LLVM_ABI bool isTokenLikeTy() const;\n   238→\n   239→  /// True if this is an instance of IntegerType.\n   240→  bool isIntegerTy() const { return getTypeID() == IntegerTyID; }\n   241→\n   242→  /// Return true if this is an IntegerType of the given width.\n   243→  LLVM_ABI bool isIntegerTy(unsigned Bitwidth) const;\n   244→\n   245→  /// Return true if this is an integer type or a vector of integer types.\n   246→  bool isIntOrIntVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isIntegerTy(); }\n   256→\n   257→  /// True if this is an instance of FunctionType.\n   258→  bool isFunctionTy() const { return getTypeID() == FunctionTyID; }\n   259→\n   260→  /// True if this is an instance of StructType.\n   261→  bool isStructTy() const { return getTypeID() == StructTyID; To get the\n   309→  /// actual size for a particular target, it is reasonable to use the\n   310→  /// DataLayout subsystem to do this.\n   311→  bool isSized(SmallPtrSetImpl<Type*> *Visited = nullptr) const {\n   312→    // If it's a primitive, it is always sized.\n   313→    if (getTypeID() == IntegerTyID || isFloatingPointTy() ||\n   314→        getTypeID() == PointerTyID || getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID)\n   315→      return true;\n   316→    // If it is not something that can have a size (e.g. a function or label),\n   317→    // it doesn't have a size.\n   318→    if (getTypeID() != StructTyID && getTypeID() != ArrayTyID &&\n   319→        !isVectorTy() && getTypeID() != TargetExtTyID)\n   320→      return false;\n   321→    // Otherwise we have to try harder to decide.\n   322→    return isSizedDerivedType(Visited);\n   323→  }\n   324→\n   325→  /// Return the basic size of this type if it is a primitive type. For more \"Type\"\n// stuff, look in DerivedTypes.h.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_IR_TYPE_H\n#define LLVM_IR_TYPE_H\n\n#include \"llvm/ADT/ArrayRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/CBindingWrapping.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Casting.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/TypeSize.h\"\n#include <cassert>\n#include <cstdint>\n#include <iterator>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\nclass IntegerType;\nstruct fltSemantics;\nclass LLVMContext;\nclass PointerType;\nclass raw_ostream;\nclass StringRef;\ntemplate <typename PtrType> class SmallPtrSetImpl;\n\n/// The instances of the Type class are immutable: once they are created,\n/// they are never changed.  Also note that only one instance of a particular\n/// type is ever created.  Thus seeing if two types are equal is a matter of\n/// doing a trivial pointer comparison. To enforce that no two equal instances\n/// are created, Type instances can only be created via static factory methods\n/// in class Type and in derived classes.  Once allocated, Types are never\n/// free'd.\n///\nclass Type {\npublic:\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  /// Definitions of all of the base types for the Type system.  Based on this\n  /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\n  /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\n  /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\n  /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\n  ///\n  enum TypeID {\n    // PrimitiveTypes\n    HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\n    BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\n    FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\n    DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\n    X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\n    FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\n    PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\n    VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\n    LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\n    MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\n    X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\n    TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\n\n    // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\n    IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\n    FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\n    PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\n    StructTyID,         ///< Structures\n    ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\n    FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\n    ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\n    TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\n    TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\n  };\n\nprivate:\n  /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n  LLVMContext &Context;\n\n  TypeID   ID : 8;            // The current base type of this type.\n  unsigned SubclassData : 24; // Space for subclasses to store data.\n                              // Note that this should be synchronized with\n                              // MAX_INT_BITS value in IntegerType class.\n\nprotected:\n  friend class LLVMContextImpl;\n\n  explicit Type(LLVMContext &C, TypeID tid)\n    : Context(C), ID(tid), SubclassData(0) {}\n  ~Type() = default;\n\n  unsigned getSubclassData() const { return SubclassData; }\n\n  void setSubclassData(unsigned val) {\n    SubclassData = val;\n    // Ensure we don't have any accidental truncation.\n    assert(getSubclassData() == val && \"Subclass data too large for field\");\n  }\n\n  /// Keeps track of how many Type*'s there are in the ContainedTys list.\n  unsigned NumContainedTys = 0;\n\n  /// A pointer to the array of Types contained by this Type. For example, this\n  /// includes the arguments of a function type, the elements of a structure,\n  /// the pointee of a pointer, the element type of an array, etc. This pointer\n  /// may be 0 for types that don't contain other types (Integer, Double,\n  /// Float).\n  Type * const *ContainedTys = nullptr;\n\npublic:\n  /// Print the current type.\n  /// Omit the type details if \\p NoDetails == true.\n  /// E.g., let %st = type { i32, i16 }\n  /// When \\p NoDetails is true, we only print %st.\n  /// Put differently, \\p NoDetails prints the type as if\n  /// inlined with the operands when printing an instruction.\n  LLVM_ABI void print(raw_ostream &O, bool IsForDebug = false,\n                      bool NoDetails = false) const;\n\n  LLVM_ABI void dump() const;\n\n  /// Return the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n  LLVMContext &getContext() const { return Context; }\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Accessors for working with types.\n  //\n\n  /// Return the type id for the type. This will return one of the TypeID enum\n  /// elements defined above.\n  TypeID getTypeID() const { return ID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'void'.\n  bool isVoidTy() const { return getTypeID() == VoidTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'half', a 16-bit IEEE fp type.\n  bool isHalfTy() const { return getTypeID() == HalfTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'bfloat', a 16-bit bfloat type.\n  bool isBFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a 16-bit float type.\n  bool is16bitFPTy() const {\n    return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID || getTypeID() == HalfTyID;\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'float', a 32-bit IEEE fp type.\n  bool isFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == FloatTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'double', a 64-bit IEEE fp type.\n  bool isDoubleTy() const { return getTypeID() == DoubleTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is x86 long double.\n  bool isX86_FP80Ty() const { return getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'fp128'.\n  bool isFP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == FP128TyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is powerpc long double.\n  bool isPPC_FP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a well-behaved IEEE-like type, which has a IEEE\n  /// compatible layout, and does not have non-IEEE values, such as x86_fp80's\n  /// unnormal values.\n  bool isIEEELikeFPTy() const {\n    switch (getTypeID()) {\n    case DoubleTyID:\n    case FloatTyID:\n    case HalfTyID:\n    case BFloatTyID:\n    case FP128TyID:\n      return true;\n    default:\n      return false;\n    }\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is one of the floating-point types\n  bool isFloatingPointTy() const {\n    return isIEEELikeFPTy() || getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID ||\n           getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\n  }\n\n  /// Returns true if this is a floating-point type that is an unevaluated sum\n  /// of multiple floating-point units.\n  /// An example of such a type is ppc_fp128, also known as double-double, which\n  /// consists of two IEEE 754 doubles.\n  bool isMultiUnitFPType() const {\n    return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\n  }\n\n  LLVM_ABI const fltSemantics &getFltSemantics() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is X86 AMX.\n  bool isX86_AMXTy() const { return getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a target extension type.\n  bool isTargetExtTy() const { return getTypeID() == TargetExtTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a target extension type with a scalable layout.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTargetExtTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is a type whose size is a known multiple of vscale.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTy(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type is or contains a target extension type that\n  /// disallows being used as a global.\n  LLVM_ABI bool\n  containsNonGlobalTargetExtType(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n  LLVM_ABI bool containsNonGlobalTargetExtType() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type is or contains a target extension type that\n  /// disallows being used as a local.\n  LLVM_ABI bool\n  containsNonLocalTargetExtType(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n  LLVM_ABI bool containsNonLocalTargetExtType() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is a FP type or a vector of FP.\n  bool isFPOrFPVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isFloatingPointTy(); }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'label'.\n  bool isLabelTy() const { return getTypeID() == LabelTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'metadata'.\n  bool isMetadataTy() const { return getTypeID() == MetadataTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'token'.\n  bool isTokenTy() const { return getTypeID() == TokenTyID; }\n\n  /// Returns true if this is 'token' or a token-like target type.s\n  LLVM_ABI bool isTokenLikeTy() const;\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of IntegerType.\n  bool isIntegerTy() const { return getTypeID() == IntegerTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is an IntegerType of the given width.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isIntegerTy(unsigned Bitwidth) const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is an integer type or a vector of integer types.\n  bool isIntOrIntVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isIntegerTy(); }\n\n  /// Return true if this is an integer type or a vector of integer types of\n  /// the given width.\n  bool isIntOrIntVectorTy(unsigned BitWidth) const {\n    return getScalarType()->isIntegerTy(BitWidth);\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is an integer type or a pointer type.\n  bool isIntOrPtrTy() const { return isIntegerTy() || isPointerTy(); }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of FunctionType.\n  bool isFunctionTy() const { return getTypeID() == FunctionTyID; }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of StructType.\n  bool isStructTy() const { return getTypeID() == StructTyID; }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of ArrayType.\n  bool isArrayTy() const { return getTypeID() == ArrayTyID; }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of PointerType.\n  bool isPointerTy() const { return getTypeID() == PointerTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a pointer type or a vector of pointer types.\n  bool isPtrOrPtrVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isPointerTy(); }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of VectorType.\n  inline bool isVectorTy() const {\n    return getTypeID() == ScalableVectorTyID || getTypeID() == FixedVectorTyID;\n  }\n\n  // True if this is an instance of TargetExtType of RISC-V vector tuple.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isRISCVVectorTupleTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type could be converted with a lossless BitCast to\n  /// type 'Ty'. For example, i8* to i32*. BitCasts are valid for types of the\n  /// same size only where no re-interpretation of the bits is done.\n  /// Determine if this type could be losslessly bitcast to Ty\n  LLVM_ABI bool canLosslesslyBitCastTo(Type *Ty) const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type is empty, that is, it has no elements or all of\n  /// its elements are empty.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isEmptyTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if the type is \"first class\", meaning it is a valid type for a\n  /// Value.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isFirstClassType() const;\n\n  /// Return true if the type is a valid type for a register in codegen. This\n  /// includes all first-class types except struct and array types.\n  bool isSingleValueType() const {\n    return isFloatingPointTy() || isIntegerTy() || isPointerTy() ||\n           isVectorTy() || isX86_AMXTy() || isTargetExtTy();\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if the type is an aggregate type. This means it is valid as\n  /// the first operand of an insertvalue or extractvalue instruction. This\n  /// includes struct and array types, but does not include vector types.\n  bool isAggregateType() const {\n    return getTypeID() == StructTyID || getTypeID() == ArrayTyID;\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if it makes sense to take the size of this type. To get the\n  /// actual size for a particular target, it is reasonable to use the\n  /// DataLayout subsystem to do this.\n  bool isSized(SmallPtrSetImpl<Type*> *Visited = nullptr) const {\n    // If it's a primitive, it is always sized.\n    if (getTypeID() == IntegerTyID || isFloatingPointTy() ||\n        getTypeID() == PointerTyID || getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID)\n      return true;\n    // If it is not something that can have a size (e.g. a function or label),\n    // it doesn't have a size.\n    if (getTypeID() != StructTyID && getTypeID() != ArrayTyID &&\n        !isVectorTy() && getTypeID() != TargetExtTyID)\n      return false;\n    // Otherwise we have to try harder to decide.\n    return isSizedDerivedType(Visited);\n  }\n\n  /// Return the basic size of this type if it is a primitive type. These are\n  /// fixed by LLVM and are not target-dependent.\n  /// This will return zero if the type does not have a size or is not a\n  /// primitive type.\n  ///\n  /// If this is a scalable vector type, the scalable property will be set and\n  /// the runtime size will be a positive integer multiple of the base size.\n  ///\n  /// Note that this may not reflect the size of memory allocated for an\n  /// instance of the type or the number of bytes that are written when an\n  /// instance of the type is stored to memory. The DataLayout class provides\n  /// additional query functions to provide this information.\n  ///\n  LLVM_ABI TypeSize getPrimitiveSizeInBits() const LLVM_READONLY;\n\n  /// If this is a vector type, return the getPrimitiveSizeInBits value for the\n  /// element type. Otherwise return the getPrimitiveSizeInBits value for this\n  /// type.\n  LLVM_ABI unsigned getScalarSizeInBits() const LLVM_READONLY;\n\n  /// Return the width of the mantissa of this type. This is only valid on\n  /// floating-point types. If the FP type does not have a stable mantissa (e.g.\n  /// ppc long double), this method returns -1.\n  LLVM_ABI int getFPMantissaWidth() const;\n\n  /// If this is a vector type, return the element type, otherwise return\n  /// 'this'.\n  inline Type *getScalarType() const {\n    if (isVectorTy())\n      return getContainedType(0);\n    return const_cast<Type *>(this);\n  }\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Type Iteration support.\n  //\n  using subtype_iterator = Type * const *;\n\n  subtype_iterator subtype_begin() const { return ContainedTys; }\n  subtype_iterator subtype_end() const { return &ContainedTys[NumContainedTys];}\n  ArrayRef<Type*> subtypes() const {\n    return ArrayRef(subtype_begin(), subtype_end());\n  }\n\n  using subtype_reverse_iterator = std::reverse_iterator<subtype_iterator>;\n\n  subtype_reverse_iterator subtype_rbegin() const {\n    return subtype_reverse_iterator(subtype_end());\n  }\n  subtype_reverse_iterator subtype_rend() const {\n    return subtype_reverse_iterator(subtype_begin());\n  }\n\n  /// This method is used to implement the type iterator (defined at the end of\n  /// the file). For derived types, this returns the types 'contained' in the\n  /// derived type.\n  Type *getContainedType(unsigned i) const {\n    assert(i < NumContainedTys && \"Index out of range!\");\n    return ContainedTys[i];\n  }\n\n  /// Return the number of types in the derived type.\n  unsigned getNumContainedTypes() const { return NumContainedTys; }\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Helper methods corresponding to subclass methods.  This forces a cast to\n  // the specified subclass and calls its accessor.  \"getArrayNumElements\" (for\n  // example) is shorthand for cast<ArrayType>(Ty)->getNumElements().  This is\n  // only intended to cover the core methods that are frequently used, helper\n  // methods should not be added here.\n\n  LLVM_ABI inline unsigned getIntegerBitWidth() const;\n\n  LLVM_ABI inline Type *getFunctionParamType(unsigned i) const;\n  LLVM_ABI inline unsigned getFunctionNumParams() const;\n  LLVM_ABI inline bool isFunctionVarArg() const;\n\n  LLVM_ABI inline StringRef getStructName() const;\n  LLVM_ABI inline unsigned getStructNumElements() const;\n  LLVM_ABI inline Type *getStructElementType(unsigned N) const;\n\n  LLVM_ABI inline uint64_t getArrayNumElements() const;\n\n  Type *getArrayElementType() const {\n    assert(getTypeID() == ArrayTyID);\n    return ContainedTys[0];\n  }\n\n  LLVM_ABI inline StringRef getTargetExtName() const;\n\n  /// Given vector type, change the element type,\n  /// whilst keeping the old number of elements.\n  /// For non-vectors simply returns \\p EltTy.\n  LLVM_ABI inline Type *getWithNewType(Type *EltTy) const;\n\n  /// Given an integer or vector type, change the lane bitwidth to NewBitwidth,\n  /// whilst keeping the old number of lanes.\n  LLVM_ABI inline Type *getWithNewBitWidth(unsigned NewBitWidth) const;\n\n  /// Given scalar/vector integer type, returns a type with elements twice as\n  /// wide as in the original type. For vectors, preserves element count.\n  LLVM_ABI inline Type *getExtendedType() const;\n\n  /// Get the address space of this pointer or pointer vector type.\n  LLVM_ABI inline unsigned getPointerAddressSpace() const;\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Static members exported by the Type class itself.  Useful for getting\n  // instances of Type.\n  //\n\n  /// Return a type based on an identifier.\n  LLVM_ABI static Type *getPrimitiveType(LLVMContext &C, TypeID IDNumber);\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // These are the builtin types that are always available.\n  //\n  LLVM_ABI static Type *getVoidTy(LLVMContext &C);\n *getInt64Ty(LLVMContext &C);\n  LLVM_ABI static IntegerType *getInt128Ty(LLVMContext &C);\n  template <typename ScalarTy> static Type *getScalarTy(LLVMContext &C) {\n    int noOfBits = sizeof(ScalarTy) * CHAR_BIT;\n    if (std::is_integral<ScalarTy>::value) {\n      return (Type*) Type::getIntNTy(C, noOfBits);\n    } else if (std::is_floating_point<ScalarTy>::value) {\n      switch These are things like \"arrays of x\" or \"structure of x, y, z\" or\n// \"function returning x taking (y,z) as parameters\", etc...\n//\n// The implementations of these classes live in the Type.cpp file.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_IR_DERIVEDTYPES_H\n#define LLVM_IR_DERIVEDTYPES_H\n\n#include \"llvm/ADT/ArrayRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/IR/Type.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Casting.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/TypeSize.h\"\n#include <cassert>\n#include <cstdint>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\nclass Value;\nclass APInt;\nclass LLVMContext;\ntemplate <typename T> class Expected;\nclass Error;\n\n/// Class to represent integer types. Note that this class is also used to\n/// represent the built-in integer types: Int1Ty, Int8Ty, Int16Ty, Int32Ty and\n/// Int64Ty.\n/// Integer representation type\nclass IntegerType : public Type {\n  friend class LLVMContextImpl;\n\nprotected:\n  explicit IntegerType(LLVMContext &C, unsigned NumBits) : Type(C, IntegerTyID){\n    setSubclassData(NumBits);\n  }\n\npublic:\n  /// This enum is just used to hold constants we need for IntegerType.\n  enum {\n    MIN_INT_BITS = 1,        ///< Minimum number of bits that can be specified\n    MAX_INT_BITS = (1<<23)   ///< Maximum number of bits that can be specified\n      ///< Note that bit width is stored in the Type classes SubclassData field\n      ///< which has 24 bits. SelectionDAG type legalization can require a\n      ///< power of 2 IntegerType, so limit to the largest representable power\n      ///< of 2, 8388608.\n  };\n\n  /// This static method is the primary way of constructing an IntegerType.\n  /// If an IntegerType with the same NumBits value was previously instantiated,\n  /// that instance will be returned. Otherwise a new one will be created. Only\n  /// one instance with a given NumBits value is ever created.\n  /// Get or create an IntegerType instance.\n  LLVM_ABI static IntegerType *get(LLVMContext &C, unsigned NumBits);\n\n  /// Returns type twice as wide the input type.\n  IntegerType *getExtendedType() const {\n    return Type::getIntNTy(getContext(), 2 * getScalarSizeInBits());\n  }\n\n  /// Get the number of bits in this IntegerType\n  unsigned getBitWidth() const { return getSubclassData(); }\n\n  /// Return a bitmask with ones set for all of the bits that can be set by an\n  /// unsigned version of this type. This is 0xFF for i8, 0xFFFF for i16, etc.\n  uint64_t getBitMask() const {\n    return ~uint64_t(0UL) >> (64-getBitWidth());\n  }\n\n  /// Return a uint64_t with just the most significant bit set (the sign bit, if\n  /// the value is treated as a signed number).\n  uint64_t getSignBit() const {\n    return 1ULL << (getBitWidth()-1);\n  }\n\n  /// For example, this is 0xFF for an 8 bit integer, 0xFFFF for i16, etc.\n  /// @returns a bit mask with ones set for all the bits of this type.\n  /// Get a bit mask for this type.\n  LLVM_ABI APInt getMask() const;\n\n  /// Methods for support type inquiry through isa, cast, and dyn_cast.\n  static bool classof(const Type *T) {\n    return T->getTypeID() == IntegerTyID;\n  }\n};\n\nunsigned Type::getIntegerBitWidth() const {\n  return cast<IntegerType>(this)->getBitWidth();\n}\n\n/// Class to represent function types\n///\nclass FunctionType : public Type {\n  FunctionType(Type *Result, ArrayRef<Type*> Params, bool IsVarArgs);\n\npublic:\n  FunctionType(const FunctionType &) = delete;\n  FunctionType &operator=(const FunctionType &) = delete;\n\n  /// This static method is the primary way of constructing a FunctionType.\n  LLVM_ABI static FunctionType *get(Type *Result, ArrayRef<Type *> Params,\n                                    bool isVarArg);\n\n  /// Create a FunctionType taking no parameters.\n  LLVM_ABI static FunctionType *get(Type *Result, bool isVarArg);\n\n  /// Return true if the specified type is valid as a return type.\n  LLVM_ABI static bool isValidReturnType(Type *RetTy);\n\n  /// Return true if the specified type is valid as an argument type.\n  LLVM_ABI static bool isValidArgumentType(Type *ArgTy);\n\n  bool isVarArg() const { return getSubclassData()!=0; }\n  Type *getReturnType() const { return ContainedTys[0]; }\n\n  using param_iterator = Type::subtype_iterator;\n\n  param_iterator param_begin() const { return ContainedTys + 1; }\n  param_iterator param_end() const { return &ContainedTys[NumContainedTys]; }\n  ArrayRef<Type *> params() const {\n    return ArrayRef(param_begin(), param_end());\n  }\n\n  /// Parameter type accessors.\n  Type *getParamType(unsigned i) const {\n    assert(i < getNumParams() && \"getParamType() out of range!\");\n    return ContainedTys[i + 1];\n  }\n\n  /// Return the number of fixed parameters this function type requires.\n  /// This does not consider varargs.\n  unsigned getNumParams() const { return NumContainedTys - 1; }\n\n  /// Methods for support type inquiry through isa, cast, and dyn_cast.\n  static bool classof(const Type *T) {\n    return T->getTypeID() == FunctionTyID;\n  }\n};\nstatic_assert(alignof(FunctionType) >= alignof(Type *),\n              \"Alignment sufficient for objects appended to FunctionType\");\n\nbool Type::isFunctionVarArg() const {\n  return cast<FunctionType>(this)->isVarArg();\n}\n\nType *Type::getFunctionParamType(unsigned i) const {\n  return cast<FunctionType>(this)->getParamType(i);\n}\n\nunsigned Type::getFunctionNumParams() const {\n  return cast<FunctionType>(this)->getNumParams();\n}\n\n/// A handy container for a FunctionType+Callee-pointer pair, which can be\n/// passed around as a single entity. This assists in replacing the use of\n/// PointerType::getElementType() to access the function's type, since that's\n/// slated for removal as part of the [opaque pointer types] project.\nclass FunctionCallee {\npublic:\n  // Allow implicit conversion from types which have a getFunctionType member\n  // (e.g. Function and InlineAsm).\n  template <typename T, typename U = decltype(&T::getFunctionType)>\n  FunctionCallee(T *Fn)\n      : FnTy(Fn ? Fn->getFunctionType() : nullptr), Callee(Fn) {}\n\n  FunctionCallee(FunctionType *FnTy, Value *Callee)\n      : FnTy(FnTy), Callee(Callee) {\n    assert((FnTy == nullptr) == (Callee == nullptr));\n  }\n\n  FunctionCallee(std::nullptr_t) {}\n\n  FunctionCallee() = default;\n\n  FunctionType *getFunctionType() { return FnTy; }\n\n  Value *getCallee() { return Callee; }\n\n  explicit operator bool() { return Callee; }\n\nprivate:\n  FunctionType *FnTy = nullptr;\n  Value *Callee = nullptr;\n};\n\n/// Class to represent struct types. All\n/// synchronization scope IDs that LLVM has special knowledge of are listed\n/// here.  Additionally, this scheme allows LLVM to efficiently check for\n/// specific synchronization scope ID without comparing strings.\nenum {\n  /// Synchronized with respect to signal handlers executing in the same thread.\n  SingleThread = 0,\n\n  /// Synchronized with respect to all concurrently executing threads.\n  System = 1\n};\n\n} // end namespace SyncScope\n\n/// This is an important class for using LLVM in a threaded context.  It\n/// (opaquely) owns and manages the core \"global\" data of LLVM's core\n/// infrastructure, including the type and constant uniquing tables.\n/// LLVMContext itself provides no locking guarantees, so you should be careful\n/// to have one context per thread.\nclass LLVMContext {\npublic:\n  LLVMContextImpl *const pImpl;\n  LLVM_ABI LLVMContext();\n  LLVMContext(const LLVMContext &) = delete;\n  LLVMContext &operator=(const LLVMContext &) = delete;\n  LLVM_ABI ~LLVMContext();\n\n  // Pinned metadata names, which always have the same value.  This is a\n  // compile-time performance optimization, not a correctness optimization.\n  enum : unsigned {\n#define LLVM_FIXED_MD_KIND(EnumID, Name, Value) EnumID = Value,\n#include \"llvm/IR/FixedMetadataKinds.def\"\n#undef LLVM_FIXED_MD_KIND\n  };\n\n  /// Known operand bundle tag IDs, which always have the same value.  All\n  /// operand bundle tags that LLVM has special knowledge of are listed here.\n  /// Additionally, this scheme allows LLVM to efficiently check for specific\n  /// operand bundle tags without comparing strings. Keep this in sync with\n  /// LLVMContext::LLVMContext().\n  enum : unsigned {\n    OB_deopt = 0,                  // \"deopt\"\n    OB_funclet = 1,                // \"funclet\"\n    OB_gc_transition = 2,          // \"gc-transition\"\n    OB_cfguardtarget = 3,          // \"cfguardtarget\"\n    OB_preallocated = 4,           // \"preallocated\"\n    OB_gc_live = 5,                // \"gc-live\"\n    OB_clang_arc_attachedcall = 6, // \"clang.arc.attachedcall\"\n    OB_ptrauth = 7,                // \"ptrauth\"\n    OB_kcfi = 8,                   // \"kcfi\"\n    OB_convergencectrl = 9,        // \"convergencectrl\"\n    OB_align = 10,                 // \"align\"\n    OB_deactivation_symbol = 11,   // \"deactivation-symbol\"\n    OB_LastBundleID = OB_deactivation_symbol\n  };\n\n  /// getMDKindID - Return a unique non-zero ID for the specified metadata kind.\n  /// This ID is uniqued across modules in the current LLVMContext.\n  LLVM_ABI unsigned getMDKindID(StringRef Name) const;\n\n  /// getMDKindNames - Populate client supplied SmallVector with the name for\n  /// custom metadata IDs registered in this LLVMContext.\n  LLVM_ABI void getMDKindNames(SmallVectorImpl<StringRef> &Result) const;\n\n  /// getOperandBundleTags - Populate client supplied SmallVector with the\n  /// bundle tags registered in this LLVMContext.  The bundle tags are ordered\n  /// by increasing bundle IDs.\n  /// \\see LLVMContext::getOperandBundleTagID\n  LLVM_ABI void getOperandBundleTags(SmallVectorImpl<StringRef> &Result) const;\n\n  /// getOrInsertBundleTag - Returns the Tag to use for an operand bundle of\n  /// name TagName.\n  LLVM_ABI StringMapEntry<uint32_t> *\n  getOrInsertBundleTag(StringRef TagName) const;\n\n  /// getOperandBundleTagID - Maps a bundle tag to an integer ID.  Every bundle\n  /// tag registered with an LLVMContext has an unique ID.\n  LLVM_ABI uint32_t getOperandBundleTagID(StringRef Tag) const;\n\n  /// getOrInsertSyncScopeID - Maps synchronization scope name to\n  /// synchronization scope ID.  Every synchronization scope registered with\n  /// LLVMContext has unique ID except pre-defined ones.\n  LLVM_ABI SyncScope::ID getOrInsertSyncScopeID(StringRef SSN);\n\n  /// getSyncScopeNames - Populates client supplied SmallVector with\n  /// synchronization scope names registered with LLVMContext.  Synchronization\n  /// scope names are ordered by increasing synchronization scope IDs.\n  LLVM_ABI void getSyncScopeNames(SmallVectorImpl<StringRef> &SSNs) const;\n\n  /// getSyncScopeName - Returns the name of a SyncScope::ID\n  /// registered with LLVMContext, if any.\n  LLVM_ABI std::optional<StringRef> getSyncScopeName(SyncScope::ID Id) const;\n\n  /// Define the GC for a function\n  LLVM_ABI void setGC(const Function &Fn, std::string GCName);\n\n  /// Return the GC for a function\n  LLVM_ABI const std::string &getGC(const Function &Fn);\n\n  /// Remove the GC for a function\n  LLVM_ABI void deleteGC(const Function &Fn);\n","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":386}}}

static EVT getVectorVT(LLVMContext &Context, EVT VT, ElementCount EC) {\n    85→      MVT M = MVT::getVectorVT(VT.V, EC);\n    86→      if (M.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n    87→ the element type converted to an integer type with the same\n    93→    /// bitwidth.\n    94→    EVT changeVectorElementTypeToInteger() const {\n    95→      if (isSimple())\n    96→        return match ourselves\n   101→    /// with the exception of the element type that is chosen by the caller.\n   102→    EVT changeVectorElementType(LLVMContext &Context, EVT EltVT) const {\n   103→      if This allows the target specific behavior\n// of instructions to be described to target independent passes.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_CODEGEN_VALUETYPES_H\n#define LLVM_CODEGEN_VALUETYPES_H\n\n#include \"llvm/CodeGenTypes/MachineValueType.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/MathExtras.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/TypeSize.h\"\n#include <cassert>\n#include <cstdint>\n#include <string>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\n  class LLVMContext;\n  class Type;\n  struct fltSemantics;\n\n  /// Extended Value Type. Capable of holding value types which are not native\n  /// for any processor (such as the i12345 type), as well as the types an MVT\n  /// can represent.\n  struct EVT {\n  private:\n    MVT V = MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE;\n    Type *LLVMTy = nullptr;\n\n  public:\n    constexpr EVT() = default;\n    constexpr EVT(MVT::SimpleValueType SVT) : V(SVT) {}\n    constexpr EVT(MVT S) : V(S) {}\n\n    bool operator==(EVT VT) const {\n      return !(*this != VT);\n    }\n    bool operator!=(EVT VT) const {\n      if (V.SimpleTy != VT.V.SimpleTy)\n        return true;\n      if (V.SimpleTy == MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return LLVMTy != VT.LLVMTy;\n      return false;\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents a floating-point type with the given\n    /// number of bits. There are two floating-point types with 128 bits - this\n    /// returns f128 rather than ppcf128.\n    static EVT getFloatingPointVT(unsigned BitWidth) {\n      return MVT::getFloatingPointVT(BitWidth);\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents an integer with the given number of\n    /// bits.\n    static EVT getIntegerVT(LLVMContext &Context, unsigned BitWidth) {\n      MVT M = MVT::getIntegerVT(BitWidth);\n      if (M.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return M;\n      return getExtendedIntegerVT(Context, BitWidth);\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents a vector NumElements in length, where\n    /// each element is of type VT.\n    static EVT getVectorVT(LLVMContext &Context, EVT VT, unsigned NumElements,\n                           bool IsScalable = false) {\n      MVT M = MVT::getVectorVT(VT.V, NumElements, IsScalable);\n      if (M.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return M;\n      return getExtendedVectorVT(Context, VT, NumElements, IsScalable);\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents a vector EC.Min elements in length,\n    /// where each element is of type VT.\n    static EVT getVectorVT(LLVMContext &Context, EVT VT, ElementCount EC) {\n      MVT M = MVT::getVectorVT(VT.V, EC);\n      if (M.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return M;\n      return getExtendedVectorVT(Context, VT, EC);\n    }\n\n    /// Return a vector with the same number of elements as this vector, but\n    /// with the element type converted to an integer type with the same\n    /// bitwidth.\n    EVT changeVectorElementTypeToInteger() const {\n      if (isSimple())\n        return getSimpleVT().changeVectorElementTypeToInteger();\n      return changeExtendedVectorElementTypeToInteger();\n    }\n\n    /// Return a VT for a vector type whose attributes match ourselves\n    /// with the exception of the element type that is chosen by the caller.\n    EVT changeVectorElementType(LLVMContext &Context, EVT EltVT) const {\n      if (isSimple() && EltVT.isSimple()) {\n        MVT M = MVT::getVectorVT(EltVT.getSimpleVT(), getVectorElementCount());\n        if (M != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n          return M;\n      }\n      return getVectorVT(Context, EltVT, getVectorElementCount());\n    }\n\n    /// Return a VT for a type whose attributes match ourselves with the\n    /// exception of the element type that is chosen by the caller.\n    EVT changeElementType(LLVMContext &Context, EVT EltVT) const {\n      EltVT = EltVT.getScalarType();\n      return isVector() ? changeVectorElementType(Context, EltVT) : EltVT;\n    }\n\n    /// Return the type converted to an equivalently sized integer or vector\n    /// with integer element type. Similar to changeVectorElementTypeToInteger,\n    /// but also handles scalars.\n    EVT changeTypeToInteger() const {\n      if (isVector())\n        return changeVectorElementTypeToInteger();\n\n      if (isSimple())\n        return getSimpleVT().changeTypeToInteger();\n      return changeExtendedTypeToInteger();\n    }\n\n    /// Test if the given EVT has zero size, this will fail if called on a\n    /// scalable type\n    bool isZeroSized() const {\n      return getSizeInBits().isZero();\n    }\n\n    /// Test if the given EVT is simple (as opposed to being extended).\n    bool isSimple() const {\n      return V.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE;\n    }\n\n    /// Test if the given EVT is extended (as opposed to being simple).\n    bool isExtended() const {\n      return !isSimple();\n    }\n\n    /// Return true if this is a FP or a vector FP type.\n    bool isFloatingPoint() const {\n      return isSimple() ? This is a private interface\n// shared between the code that implements the SelectionDAG::LegalizeTypes\n// method.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_LIB_CODEGEN_SELECTIONDAG_LEGALIZETYPES_H\n#define LLVM_LIB_CODEGEN_SELECTIONDAG_LEGALIZETYPES_H\n\n#include \"MatchContext.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n#include \"llvm/CodeGen/SelectionDAG.h\"\n#include \"llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n/// This takes an arbitrary SelectionDAG as input and hacks on it until only\n/// value types the target machine can handle are left. This involves promoting\n/// small sizes to large sizes or splitting up large values into small values.\n///\nclass LLVM_LIBRARY_VISIBILITY DAGTypeLegalizer {\n  const TargetLowering &TLI;\n  SelectionDAG &DAG;\npublic:\n  /// This pass uses the NodeId on the SDNodes to hold information about the\n  /// state of the node. The enum has all the values.\n  enum NodeIdFlags {\n    /// All operands have been processed, so this node is ready to be handled.\n    ReadyToProcess = 0,\n\n    /// This is a new node, not before seen, that was created in the process of\n    /// legalizing some other node.\n    NewNode = -1,\n\n    /// This node's ID needs to be set to the number of its unprocessed\n    /// operands.\n    Unanalyzed = -2,\n\n    /// This is a node that has already been processed.\n    Processed = -3\n\n    // 1+ - This is a node which has this many unprocessed operands.\n  };\nprivate:\n\n  /// This is a bitvector that contains two bits for each simple value type,\n  /// where the two bits correspond to the LegalizeAction enum from\n  /// TargetLowering. This can be queried with \"getTypeAction(VT)\".\n  TargetLowering::ValueTypeActionImpl ValueTypeActions;\n\n  /// Return how we should legalize values of this type.\n  TargetLowering::LegalizeTypeAction getTypeAction(EVT VT) const {\n    return TLI.getTypeAction(*DAG.getContext(), VT);\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this type is legal on this target.\n  bool isTypeLegal(EVT VT) const {\n    return TLI.getTypeAction(*DAG.getContext(), VT) == TargetLowering::TypeLegal;\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a simple legal type.\n  bool isSimpleLegalType(EVT VT) const {\n    return VT.isSimple() && TLI.isTypeLegal(VT);\n  }\n\n  EVT getSetCCResultType(EVT VT) const {\n    return TLI.getSetCCResultType(DAG.getDataLayout(), *DAG.getContext(), VT);\n  }\n\n  /// Pretend all of this node's results are legal.\n  bool IgnoreNodeResults(SDNode *N) const {\n    return N->getOpcode() == ISD::TargetConstant ||\n           N->getOpcode() == ISD::Register;\n  }\n\n  // Bijection from SDValue to unique id. As each created node gets a\n  // new id we do not need to worry about reuse expunging.  Should we\n  // run out of ids, we can do a one time expensive compactifcation.\n  typedef unsigned TableId;\n\n  TableId NextValueId = 1;\n\n  SmallDenseMap<SDValue, TableId, 8> ValueToIdMap;\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, SDValue, 8> IdToValueMap;\n\n  /// For integer nodes that are below legal width, this map indicates what\n  /// promoted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> PromotedIntegers;\n\n  /// For integer nodes that need to be expanded this map indicates which\n  /// operands are the expanded version of the input.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> ExpandedIntegers;\n\n  /// For floating-point nodes converted to integers of the same size, this map\n  /// indicates the converted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> SoftenedFloats;\n\n  /// For floating-point nodes that have a smaller precision than the smallest\n  /// supported precision, this map indicates what promoted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> PromotedFloats;\n\n  /// For floating-point nodes that have a smaller precision than the smallest\n  /// supported precision, this map indicates the converted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> SoftPromotedHalfs;\n\n  /// For float nodes that need to be expanded this map indicates which operands\n  /// are the expanded version of the input.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> ExpandedFloats;\n\n  /// For nodes that are <1 x ty>, this map indicates the scalar value of type\n  /// 'ty' to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> ScalarizedVectors;\n\n  /// For nodes that need to be split this map indicates which operands are the\n  /// expanded version of the input.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> SplitVectors;\n\n  /// For vector nodes that need to be widened, indicates the widened value to\n  /// use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> WidenedVectors;\n\n  /// For values that have been replaced with another, indicates the replacement\n  /// value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> ReplacedValues;\n\n  /// This defines a worklist of nodes to process. In order to be pushed onto\n  /// this worklist, all operands of a node must have already been processed.\n  SmallVector<SDNode*, 128> Worklist;\n\n  TableId getTableId(SDValue V) {\n    assert(V.getNode() && \"Getting TableId on SDValue()\");\n\n    auto I = ValueToIdMap.find(V);\n    if (I != ValueToIdMap.end()) {\n      // replace if there's been a shift.\n      RemapId(I->second);\n      assert(I->second && \"All Ids should be nonzero\");\n      return I->second;\n    }\n    // Add if it's not there.","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1229}}}
